RATING: 10
A very well developed game. Definetly one of the best coops. In expert mode, it really depends of your special abilities. 

Unlike Forbidden island, where the Pilot negates almoust all of the strenghts of a diver (who is acctially a very fun adddition to the Island game!), in the Desert, you dont have a Pilot so the climber is very important and he can also take one of the other figurines with him to the mountains of sand! 

This ability is great because it makes the game more tactical and also it can save action points for other players (they save on movement). I use a combo of the climber and the Archeaologist where they both move onto a mountain in the climbers turn, and then the Archeaologist can spent all his 4 action for a very efficient sand removal operation! 

Also the explorer is a lot more important than in the Island game. He is excellent for early game exploration, where the starting sand tiles are diagonally arranged, so he may reveal 2 city tiles in one turn and may continue to do this for the next 3-4 turns (this means revealing at least 6-8 city tiles by himself).

RATING: 5
[I]tl;dr A necessary improvement on Forbidden Island, a solid overall co-op from the designer of Pandemic.[/I]
[COLOR=#CCCCFF]____________________________[/COLOR]

It's pretty clear to me that Forbidden Desert is a much improved version of Forbidden Island. There's lots more to do, and the system of locating parts of the aircraft is pretty genius. I'm glad this one is in our collection and not Island.

Basically, you are all explorers who have crashed in a desert, and must recover all the pieces of a buried aircraft to escape the desert before you run out of water. The board is made up of tiles which you will explore by excavating sand from and flipping. 

Overall, a solid co-op that is very enjoyable. Very tight with four players, we found it easier with five. It's a good game, but ultimately I found that Matt Leacock's 'alpha player' problem has dogged this one as well. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Can be a good co-op experience with the right people. I'd definitely recommend this as a casual game to play if I need to kill an hour.

RATING: 8.5
Forbidden Desert is a fantastic co-op game for these reasons:

-It is simple and streamlined
-It presents the player with tough choices 
-There is beautiful art and a clean design
-The random board set up makes for a different experience each time
-Variable player powers and difficulty levels also keeps the game fresh
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I think this is the most tense game that I own. Every turn of Forbidden Desert is a nail-biter and it only gets more critical as the game goes on. The nice thing is that the game offers only a few decisions, so that analysis paralysis never really sets in. Especially because there is rarely any way of knowing what the best course may be.

I love the way the sand piles up and the way the tiles move with the sandstorm. The theme really comes alive in this game, as players get more and more desperate to clear sand and the missing valuables become more and more buried in the ever-changing heart and heat of the desert. The deck of cards that determines whether the sun beats down upon uncovered survivors or whether the storm picks up its intensity is a cruel and feisty mistress. Eyes always go wide and passions ignite when its time to draw from it.

Forbidden Desert, while by no means an easy game, is a simple one and I would wholeheartedly recommend it for families and non-gamers. It's a perfect gateway game for those who enjoy abstract classics or puzzles. By no means should this be forbidden from your collection (especially at that price!)

RATING: 8
Get this game. Just do it. Imagine a streamlined, simplified Pandemic with great bits/pieces and unique mechanics. You can teach it to newbies within 10 minutes, and they'll feel empowered and involved due to the co-op and collaborative nature of the game. Since each role is useful and needed, even brand-new players feel like they were critical to victory.

The game has chance elements, but even so, you can trace back your plays and see where you could have made different decisions. Agency is a big part of this game, and it works wonderfully.

This is one of my go-to games for new folks to get them into the hobby. It's light enough to learn quickly, but dynamic and clever  enough to keep coming back for more.

RATING: 9
If you want to introduce friends and family to higher-caliber board games, this or the four-player Forbidden Island is one of the best places to start in my book. This one is definitely harder than Island, but I still adore both. Beautiful art and presentation (who isn't a sucker for games in tins?), terrific action-adventure movie concept, and each player playing the good and evil side of the game every turn adds to the tension and thrill.

Like with Forbidden Island, I like that the layout of the board is different nearly every time, but Desert takes it up a notch with the tiles moving every turn thanks to the sandstorm and the hidden treasure pieces also being in different locations every game. The unique player powers provide a lot of opportunity for strategy and interaction under a challenging objective. I've won plenty of three-player games, but something about the max five-player games has made victory more elusive. But we always have a blast and want to try just-one-more-time.

RATING: 8
One of the best cooperative games ever played. You have to find the missing parts of a steam punk airship in the desert and fly out. It seems easy but the tiles of desert (dunes) re constantly moving and filling up with sand blocking your movements, and even the sun can drain your powers and leave you dehydrated (unless you find the well). Easy to player and hard to master. What I did really enjoy is the fact that the difficulty of the game can be adjusted by the means of the cards drawn to move the dunes and fill them with sand.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Yes, there are similarities between this and Forbidden Island, but Forbidden Desert is nevertheless a fairly different game. Forbidden Island now feels to me like the unfinished prototype of Forbidden Desert! If you don't own either game, get Forbidden Desert. If you already own Forbidden Island and get Forbidden Desert, be warned: you'll probably trade away Forbidden Island! Although I do kinda miss the rapidly shrinking island aspect....

Although it's not my favourite co-op (Space Alert), it's probably the best co-op I've played. What I mean by that is in most co-ops, each player is assigned his or her own duty, and they go off and do it. Not so in Forbidden Desert. In Desert, you MUST be working together very closely (and usually closely on the board) since each player is very much dependent on the others for survival. That in itself makes Forbidden Desert unique, and truly cooperative.

A most beautiful game, and a considerably deeper game than Forbidden Island, while nevertheless remaining family-friendly.

In Forbidden Desert, a thematic sequel to Forbidden Island, players take on the roles of brave adventurers who must throw caution to the wind and survive both blistering heat and blustering sand in order to recover a legendary flying machine buried under an ancient desert city. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Based on many of the comments I expected this game to be a disappointment and a replica of Forbidden Island, but I was pleasantly surprised.

While the game has a number of similarities to Forbidden Island, it also has enough to differentiate it.  I particularly liked the hidden treasure aspect and the innovative way the treasure moves around as the sandstorm blankets the map.  Thematically, you do feel exposed and frustrated as the sun beats down and you race to find the treasure before your water supply runs out.

In many ways, I feel Forbidden Desert is a better game overall, but a few more plays will tell.  Either way, it is definitely enjoyable, tense and very accessible for non-gamers.

2 − 5
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This was my favorite game for a while. The ever changing board is an excellent mechanic and keeps you on your toes. The cooperative aspect of the game is well done and it always gets tense and exciting at the end when you're trying to get everyone on the ship to leave the desert. 

My only gripe with the game is the difficulty. There are four difficulty levels: Novice, normal, advanced, and legendary. My group has only been able to win on "normal" a small fraction of the time we've played. Unless you get the perfect roles and everything goes perfectly, I just don't see how casual gamers are supposed to go above the normal difficulty. 

Despite the difficulty, there is a lot of fun to be had here. If you like super challenging games, then this one is for you! Even if you're not, stick with the novice or normal difficulty and you'll have a blast. 

Pros
-components (the ship!!!)
-ever-changing mechanics
-variable roles
-strong desert theme
-excitement in flipping tiles

Cons
-almost impossible difficulty on advanced and legendary tiers
-possible alpha-player who decides everything for the whole team

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I know the classic gateway games are Ticket to Ride, Carcassonne, and Settlers of Catan, but in my very humble opinion this is the best gateway game out there. I love, love, LOVE the theme matching mechanic. I haven't played a game with a better "thematic mechanic" than the roving sand storm. It's relatively easy to teach, because most of the information in the game is hidden and randomized there is virtually no "quarterbacking" and actually, though the game feels strategic, and there are strategic elements to it, it actually plays out more tactically. I love the type of teamwork it induces in a group, again, thematic. You really do feel like a team of adventurers struggling to survive. All this and the game wraps up in 45 minutes. As for replayability, the game is hard to win, and harder the more people you add. I've yet to beat a 4 player game on novice, though I've come close enough not to be discouraged.

UPDATE: Although I still do like this game very much I'm usually not in the mood to play. There doesn't seem to be enough strategy to keep me engaged.

This is the only game I will ever give a full 10 to. Why? To skew the average rating so more people will play this game and experience its wonder. The concept of assembling a ship to escape the desert was pleasing and the fit of the components was neat. My only complaint was, why does the ship need a core and a engine? Really broke the immersion for me. 
The sandstorm mechanic can be tricky to master. It took us several playthroughs to fully grasp it, but then again we were probably drunk, thus giving us the minds of small children. Therefore, small children will enjoy this short game, assuming they don't choke on the pieces.

RATING: 7
I’m a fan of these team vs. environment board games, in the family of Pandemic, etc. This game is the brother of Forbidden Island, and between the two, I actually like this one the best, although I’ve heard many of my friends have the opposite opinion. I love the game mechanics. Not a big fan of the Meteorologist's ability, but sometimes I just throw that card out of the random character draw before the game begins.
I can only come up with one con for this game, which is that the game difficulty can swing pretty dramatically depending on chance. If the last three tiles you discover have the tunnels, for example… the game can become pretty impossible, no matter how well the team uses strategy. Or ridiculously easy, a time or two… Those games are statistical outliers though, most of the time this game is super!

RATING: 7.5
A fun co-op where you've crash landed in the desert and must search for the pieces of a mythical flying machine to get out. Each player has a differt roll. The board is made up of tiles, laid out in a 5x5 grid with one missing to represent the area with the sand storm. Players clear tiles of sand and flip them to find gear or clues to the parts' location. Players can lose by thirsting to death, getting buried in sand or the storm intensity reaching deadly levels. Game can be very tense and exciting.

RATING: 5
1 play:

There are a few problems with this game that limit it.

First, the sandstorm cards are less than totally clear about which way is up, and we often found ourselves having to redo the last set of sand movements because the card was upside down.

Second, the discovery mechanism feels arbitrary. I get that we are supposed to pretend we are finding clues about where the artifacts are buried, but this doesn't feel convincing because the locations aren't set until you uncover both location markers. Same thing for the tools you can uncover: drawing them from a pre-shuffled deck of cards makes excavation feel more like a chore than a thrilling risk.

The first time my daughter and I played Forbidden Island, we were enraptured. Not so with Forbidden Desert, even though we were looking forward to it.

RATING: 8
Wonderful co-op game! I love it as it has enough differences from Forbidden Island til keep it fresh - and very difficult to beat when playing 2-4 players.

The game is surprisingly easy to beat if you play solo with just 1 character though.

If you fear that you will get "Forbidden Island 2" then don't worry. It has two similarities: the storm tracker works the same way as FI's water rise, and you are racing against time. Besides that it is a total different gameplay and is just as intense as FI, especially when running to the ship at the end. I have lost being only ONE tile away from the landing platform; I got burned from the sun and died of thirst a few meters from the finish line.

Two BIG thumbs up for Matt Leacock! Keep making games! I love you, man!!

RATING: 5.5
Pandemic is my favorite game, and I really wanted to like this. Several plays later, and I'm still not enthused. The exploration mechanic really annoys me because, whereas in Pandemic your planning has a distinct purpose based on the board state, in FD you just flounder around until you find what you're looking for. The result is that I always feel like we just got lucky whenever we win, and were simply unlucky if we lose. I'll just stick to Pandemic, which, with the expansions, blows this out of the water both in strategy as well as in replayability. Sold.

:thumbsup: [b]POSITIVE POINTS:[/b]

++ Good, simple, light weight co-op game, with a great blend of gameplay mechanisms that fit the theme.
++ Good replayability from the different character cards and the variable storm movements.
++ Great insert that easily fits everything in its place. 
++ Variable difficulty is really easy to set up.
++ Easy to teach, fast to set-up and fast to play.


:thumbsdown: [b]NEGATIVE POINTS:[/b]

-- The gameplay somewhat always seems like the same.
-- Even though necessary, the sand tiles takes time to always stack up correctly and it can look a bit messy (our sand tiles are a bit curved so it may be worst for us than for other people).
-- Too light for us (even though you can play at a higher difficulty, choices to be made during the game always seems light).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Based on 1 play with 5 players:

It's really hard not to compare this to Pandemic. This is different enough to justify its existence, I suppose, but only just. If you already have Pandemic, it's probably not worth owning this too (especially if you have Pandemic's excellent expansions).

It's hard to tell whether there is more or less luck in this game, compared to Pandemic. There's no hero deck, so you can't, for example, continue to draw "useless" cards, but the Deck of Bad Stuff feels far more random. Sometimes you get cards that don't do anything, much to everyone's relief, but it's 100% luck of the draw. It's similar to drawing an eradicated color in Pandemic, but there it was a reward for skillful play which made it much more interesting and meaningful.

Also, it just feels like there's less to do in this game, full stop. There's less things to think about. And the theme is cool, but there are hundreds of games about "exploration" in some way so it doesn't exactly wow me. The flying ship is a rad idea, but it looks pretty ugly when built frankly. The colors of the different parts just don't come together in a nice way.

We played our first game on Normal and beat it without TOO much trouble. I'm not sure if it's easier than Pandemic (which took our group a few tries to master on normal) or I'm just better at these types of games now.

The way the game scales its difficulty makes me disinclined to try it on harder settings - I'm sure it works fine, but it's just not very interesting. The epidemics in Pandemic have a narrative and emotional weight to them that "start with less turns" just doesn't replicate, even if it makes things more tense.

It was engaging while playing, but if I happened to never play again I wouldn't feel like I'm missing out.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
I like Pandemic quite a bit but never really felt that Forbidden Island was a good game. Forbidden Desert is sort of a sequel to Forbidden Island, but it’s much, much better! Like FI, FD features a pretty simple gameplay in which you have 4 actions and then flip over some cards which do bad things. You win if you find 4 part of an ancient flying ship and get to a certain tile before any player loses all of his water, the sandstorm track reaches a high level or if there aren’t enough sand tiles left. I like coop games in which you can only win in one way but lose in several. What makes FD so much better than FI is because of its slightly more “game-y” gameplay; FI is a light family game, but FD is a little step above. The genius idea of the moving sand tiles is what I like the most about the game as you never know where you’ll be or where the tiles will be on your next turn. 

The variable player powers, the items you can find and use as free actions, the tunnels in which you can “teleport” and hide from the sun are other very cool features as is how you actually are able to pinpoint where the ship components are hidden and the fact that they can move (which can really hurt you!). It’s an easy game to teach and play, and if you think it’s too easy to win, it’s very easy to adjust the difficulty level. I’m sure it’s going to be a hit with my family as well as some of my friends who aren’t really gamers. Any game I play about 10 times in a single month is definitely a good game! So why do I only rate it a 7 you say? Well, it’s a bit too simple for my taste. It’s quick, but I would rather play Pandemic for the same kind of feeling (although the two games are certainly very different).

RATING: 7
Hopefully this isn't just a reimplementation.

Now *this* is a different game than Pandemic. Obviously inspired from it, but the presence of two ticking timers (the ever-rising sand and the ever-dwindling supplies of water) make this game even more of a thrill to play. Even better, the tiles don't disappear after being buried under heaps and heaps of sand, which means that you never feel so overwhelmed as to become desperate. And then you lose, of course, but that's just how life is, right?

RATING: 6

If you can pick up the 2013 Pandemic base game for $20, On the Brink for $25, for $45 I guess it is OK, for way less Forbidden Desert will do you.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.4
What's impressive here is Matt Leacock was able to take one of his existing games and twist it enough that it truly feels new again.  In a nutshell - if you own and like Forbidden Island, there's no reason not to get the "sequel" as well.

This time around the tiles move due to a sandstorm, and pieces can get increasingly buried under the sand.  So you can't just ignore certain tiles anymore.  Also new is water rations - if anyone runs out when the sun beats down, you lose - so knowing where the wells are is crucial.  Lastly, the pieces of your ship aren't found in one place - you have to reveal the two matching tiles and then find the piece and their intersection.

So this is a winner - I definitely will want to play it regularly.  The art theme is steampunk which is cool, but it lacks the visual wonder that I thought was so great in FI.  Other than that, as usual Gamewright has top-notch components and packaging.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
This game is quite similar to Pandemic (from the same designer), but it is nice to have both in my collection. Again, it is coop (or solo) puzzle game to solve the goal before the game eliminates you.
Here you are some adventurers wrecked on the desert and trying to find the pieces of mystery ship to survive the heat and leave the desert.
Again, you will control different characters with different powers, having four action per turn so you can move, dig a sand, excavate etc. By excavating you will get useful tools to help you with your efforts, but also some clues where the four missing parts of the ship are located.
Your goal is to find those parts and pick them up to the leaving point before you die by thirst, bury in sand or swap away by heat. 
You will find some water wells to fresh yourselves and also tunnels where you can travel through and cool yourself from devastating sun heat. 

There is some comparison to Pandemic:
- the difficulty (to win the game) is harder than Pandemic. On normal difficulty I will more often die than win
- On the other side, I believe the rules are more simple having just a few characters, just a few helpful artifacts and only one way to move. Although Pandemic is also elegant and simple by rules, this is even more newbie friendly.
- Theme is nice there. Instead of disease spread through the globe, you will try to survive on the desert full of sand dunes and sun heat. And believe me, you will feel like you are on the desert praying that the sand storm doesn't hit you and bury you under the sand. The feel of the game is pressing there again, in similar both slightly different (more personal) way. You are trying to survive yourself instead of saving the world.
- There is no board, instead of it the game takes place in 5x5 grid of game board tiles allowing to randomize the starting setup for each game. This forces you to excavate the ground finding the needed clues for the missing pieces of the plane - each game will be different.

What I like
- the way you need to find and pick up the pieces of the ship is original and funny. You will have to excavate two pieces of clues for each part of the machine and then they will tell you where the part is. Then you will need to move there and pick it up. This is like finding the cure in pandemic, you need four parts to be able to leave. Slightly different, but similar principle here
- The constant pressure. You will be dying on thirst, sand will be growing and growing so you will need a lot of time (or some nice tool) to dig some places. If there are a lot of sand, you couldn't move through, but you desperately need to move there to pick that part or to hide to the tunnel to save your ass.
- The way the sandstorm acts. Again, as in Pandemic, the desert storm will act as in real desert. Moving from there to here, leaving more sand behind and maybe even bury yourself in sand. 
- I like the puzzle aspect of the game. You will have to risk sometimes leaving your fate in hand of the destiny (pack of storm cards), but in most cases you will have to find the best way how to handle the current issue out of several possible ones.

What I dislike:
- I would prefer normal (Paper or cartoon) game box instead of the Tin one with weird shape. It is original, but it looks strange in your game shelf. The storage could be better done.
- As in Pandemic, this game can suffer from alpha player issue when one player could take control of the game telling other what is the best way what to do (I am guilty of this behavior sadly sometimes). 
- some games are just one big frustration as the luck is not present and you will just die no matter how hard you try.

RATING: 9
If Forbidden Desert costs $40+, I would not recommend it. However, you can regularly find it for sale at $20 or less, which makes it an amazing value. You get a slightly less complex but arguably equally fun co-op game compared to let's say Pandemic but for 2/3 of the price or less. 

The theme is a highlight of the game. You are a group of steam-punk adventurers trapped in a desert sandstorm and must scavenge parts to rebuild your airship to escape before the sand buries you. The game mechanism lets you do exactly these things: move around to clear sand and excavate for the four required parts while the sand tiles shift around in a random fashion and accumulate more sand. It is a race against time, just like Pandemic, but on a more personal level. And it is also a difficult game, just like Pandemic; you (and your friends) will not survive often. But when you do, you feel an incredible sense of satisfaction. To add to it, you will get to assemble a mini airship with the parts you find. These are high-quality components (the engine, for example, is actually cast in metal) that are much appreciated in such a budget-priced game.

So the value of Forbidden Desert is through the roof. You get a tense, thematic game with high-quality components for under $20.

RATING: 7
[28 Dec 2017] - 7 (2 plays, 1 recorded)
It's a light, co-op game that has a lot in common with Pandemic. Needing to discover two tiles in order to find the parts at the intersect makes the game more challenging as more tiles need to be explored. The addition of the water supply per player also adds a bit more to think about but it isn't that hard to work with. It's a fun game and one that I added to my collection specifically because it can be played with non-gamers. The co-op design takes less pressure off the inexperienced since they'll be playing on the same team as the gamers in the group.

This gives off the same vibes as Pandemic, i.e. you always feel like several things are working against you and pressuring you into quickly & efficiently completing your objectives, which is the key to making a great cooperative game. The excitement, range of options, and accessibility to new players makes it one of the best cooperative games out there.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game is one step further removed from Pandemic than was Forbidden Island. The latter retained Pandemic's mechanism of aggregating cards into one player's hand in order to capture a treasure (or cure a disease). Forbidden Desert dispenses with hands of cards in favor of moving to tiles and then flipping those to discover the parts, water, and gear you need to survive and flee the desert. I find this to be a more satisfying process and thus Forbidden Desert to be a better game than its predecessor. I think Forbidden Desert is more difficult to win also, but it's close.

RATING: 6.5
Per my usual, I can't really rate too many cooperatives too high - I have trouble hitting the middle ground between oppressive alpha gaming and complete non-engagement with the game. I tend to settle for just focusing on carefully acting on my own turn, without contributing to others' turns unless queried.

That said, Forbidden Desert has a lot to enjoy in how its theme comes through in game-play. I adore the gradually piling sand and how it slows movement and, eventually, traps you beneath it. New people have trouble with the idea that the treasures aren't hidden at a specific tile until we find them - normally just have to encourage them to 'go with it.' Tends to click during the game.

It's still very very very good.

RATING: 8
Leacock's middle child?

It is interesting to see how Matt Leacock's game design evolved into Pandemic, because it's so transparent in the forbidden series.

Desert clearly improves upon Island, which for its part is a fun enough game, if not a little easy. Desert has more ways to murder you, but also adds curious mechanics like the storms movement, and steampunk themed gear cards.

The art work again is beautiful, compelling, but disappointingly superficial since there is no time to explore in this smash and grab game. 

Difficulty is very easy to ramp up. My wife and I went from being pretty cocky, to dead AF every time we play with just one bump in level. This may be owing to the layout of the tiles, the vulnerability of our characters, whatever. Dead is dead. Victory will be that much sweeter, I suppose.

I enjoy this more than [the android version of] Pandemic, and look forward to playing it with my kid when he gets older.

RATING: N/A
Gear up for a thrilling adventure to recover a legendary flying machine buried deep in the ruins of an ancient desert city. You'll need to coordinate with your teammates and use every available resource if you hope to survive the scorching heat and relentless sandstorm. Find the flying machine and escape before you all become permanent artifacts of the forbidden desert!

In Forbidden Desert, a thematic sequel to Forbidden Island, players take on the roles of brave adventurers who must throw caution to the wind and survive both blistering heat and blustering sand in order to recover a legendary flying machine buried under an ancient desert city. While featuring cooperative gameplay similar to Forbidden Island, Forbidden Desert is a fresh, new game based around an innovative set of mechanisms such as an ever-shifting board, individual resource management, and a unique method for locating the flying machine parts.

-------------Original rating 30/5/17 Score:7
[b]Rating based on - 5+ plays, 2 player[/b]
The sequel to Forbidden Island, this game takes you on a survival mission in a burning hot desert where your helicopter has crashed. You will need to survive thirst, the blazing sun, a merciless storm and the resultant shifting sands. The Forbidden games use math in a really clever way to deliver thematic, exciting and [-]sometimes[/-] usually brutal experiences. It's probabilities all the way from the ratio of cards in the deck to the adjustable difficulty levels of the Storm Meter. 

Having played and loved Forbidden Island, I was very satisfied but my gaming partner was curious as to what this had to offer. Production quality is on par with that of Forbidden Island – high quality cards, tiles and plastic/metal components for the ship, and I heartily appreciate the fact that they included a stand for the Storm Meter as I'd had to get my own for the Waters Rising in Forbidden Island. It's quick and easy to setup and I love games in tins! The insert is great and holds everything perfectly, and the rule design is attractive yet functional. However, we came upon an ambiguous rule and that is to do with the use of the Solar Shield. It can be interpreted in two ways but the official ruling is that: [b]Solar Shield cannot be deployed after Sun Beats Down has been revealed![/b] 

Initially I was unimpressed as we won our first game on Novice quite easily. We then ramped it up to Normal and we were on our way to a decent level of difficulty, but still quite easy. We beat Elite on the first go as well which was very surprising. Our default starting setting is now Legendary. Maybe on future plays we'll try controlling two characters each as well and see if that ups the difficulty... It was easy to learn and play especially since we were already familiar with the system, but I feel it is easier than Forbidden Island where you also have the hand management aspect and have to decide which treasure clues or equipment to drop and then you curse when you finally get the last of a set....aargh!!! Here there is no hand limit so you can collect as much equipment as you'd like to help you without the agonising choice of whether to get rid of a clue or your sandbags. I also don't feel we do as much talking/co-ordinating here as most decisions seem quite obvious. You get a genuine feeling of exploration as you need to dig sand and excavate tiles to find the location of the missing ship parts, but it's also tedious working the entire grid. A hit and miss approach would not be very effective. 

Although the way the storm moves and the sand builds up is very cool and unique, I don't feel that this does anything better than Forbidden Island. I also love the Forbidden Island artwork much better plus the variety you get from all of the different island layouts. We don't need to start on anything higher than Normal as those layouts are difficult enough! I think this lack of variety would hurt Forbidden Desert and make it feel a bit same-y in the long run. This title is one that my gaming partner and I are in contention about – the exploration/discovery itch is scratched for me by Dead Men Tell No Tales, and the triangulation of the lost equipment itch is scratched by Crashland so I see no need to also have this one in the collection. Under evaluation.
[b]Status: TRADED for Times Square[/b]

RATING: N/A
Itch: co-op

For me, the good:

- The theme permeates everything in an amazing way
- Clues offer an interesting alternative to Pandemic or Forbidden Island's set collection
- I like coops

The bad

- Finding the clues feels like an exercise in "flip all the tiles before you die". While I initially liked the clues approach, its started to make me question my purchase.
- I grew up in the dessert and loathe them, so I'd prefer the look of Forbidden Island but it felt too easy and too close to Pandemic.
- I tend to prefer more real-world themes, so I probably would have preferred Flashpoint for my non-Pandemic coop.

RATING: 7
Forbidden Desert is a good gateway game into the co-op gaming universe.  The game could easily be played with families and older kids (maybe, 9-10?) and has enough substance where adults can quite happily play it.

The game has a nice cohesive theme, interesting mechanics and doesn't suffer from a fixed board layout, so it has solid replayability.

Things can get tense in later game when it comes down to the wire, co-operation and co-ordination is must!

The game may be a bit too simplistic for some, or may hit the perfect balance for lighter gamers; either way, it's one you can easily pull out to play with non-gamers.

Ez egy nagyszerű családi játék! Elkerülhetetlen, hogy összehasonlítsam a Pandemiccel. A szabályrendszere egyszerűbb, mint a Pandemicé, könnyebben befogadható társasjátékokban kevésbé rutinos játékosoknak is. 4 egyszerű akciót hajthatunk végre a körünkben, amit – a játék menetét erősen befolyásoló – megfelelő számú viharkártya felhúzása követ. A játék egyik legötletesebb része a homokfúvás, amikor is a lapkáink a viharkártyának megfelelően mozognak (és temetődnek be homokjelölőkkel). A feszültség is kisebb, mint a Pandemicben, ami nem azt jelenti, hogy nem rágjuk le a körmünket idegességünkben! Nagy pozitívum, hogy öten is játszható, bár az ideális játékoslétszám szerintem 3-4 fő. Ami elsősorban családi játékká predesztinálja, az a nagyfokú szerencse a játékban! Ez nem negatívum, csak tisztában kell lenni vele, hogy ez egy a szerencsére nagyban építő játék. A véletlenszerű lapkaelrendezés, illetve a felhúzandó viharkártyák elrendezése nagyon kedvező, illetőleg kedvezőtlen helyzetbe is hozhat bennünket pillanatok alatt! A különböző tulajdonságokkal rendelkező karakterekkel tudjuk nemileg kordában tartani az ingadozó szerencsét. Könnyű tehát elbukni a játékot, de akkor jöhet egy újabb menet! A játékidő nagyban egyezik a dobozra írttal, azaz kb. 45 perc alatt megy le egy parti. Hacsak nem pusztulunk el hamarabb a sivatagban. Szép játék, viszonylag gyors, kooperatív, élvezet minden perce!

RATING: 7.4
Resisted getting this game because thought it would be too similar to Forbidden Island.  It's true that knowing Forbidden Island is groundwork for this game, but the games are different enough that I am delighted I also own this.  

Forbidden Desert plays 5, instead of 4.  It includes features in  the game very apropos to the desert theme.  Sandstorms occur with shifting dunes, water is an issue as the sun beats down.  The metal box is a problem on my game shelf, but the components are quality & add flavor to the game.  It is harder to win and employs a different strategy, and lasts longer even though the game moves right along.  I found that more communication & cooperation between the 5 of us occurred than with Forbidden Island.  The game adjusts nicely to fewer players.  Easy to teach & remember game play.

RATING: 8.5
Forbidden Desert 禁忌沙漠 2-5(4)
Our group we always play 5P, we played it four times; twice with navigator, twice without. We lost both times without the navigator and that makes me wondering - best not jump to the conclusion too early. Regardless, we love this game, people have requested to bring this game henceforth for the rest of year, because it's that challenging! The tension gradually picks up around mid stage, and I think that's where the fun starts. The rule is not 100% clear and has some small things you might want to check on the forum first. Luck in this game is totally acceptable because the short play time and constant shift of sands fits the theme very nice. Some games you may have it easy on you with the quick-access tunnels or the dumb eye of storm that constant hitting walls, but that is all part of great fun about this game. 
+Exquisite game design
+Player power fun
+Tension building

Cons

RATING: 8.75

RATING: 2
This feels so much a skin for Matt Leacock's other cooperative designs, that I am tempted to simply refer you to my other reviews for them.
The games are cooperative, but players of varying skill levels break the game immediately, as a skilled player will either take the game over (since that player makes the best decisions) or must sit back and host the game.
The dangers that appear between turns do not feel quite so random in this particular title since they all center about the storm, but the fact that the storm cannot wrap around the board makes the game no less of a crapshoot than other similar titles.

RATING: 8
While I'm finding that I am starting to dislike the "quarterbacking" of co-op games (I want to be 100% in control of my actions), this is a fantastic solo game! Unlike some games that have awkward rule exceptions/addendums for solo play (e.g. Imperial Settlers) this one plays smoothly.

The artwork and theme are both highly tuned. I typically don't like games with lots of fiddly little parts, but I make an exception for this one (and it's still far better than others in this respect, like Small World, which I refuse to play any more). It comes in a very nice looking and feeling tin can too.

The rules and gameplay are surprisingly easy to pick up quickly given it's decidedly not a "light" game. It's good game design: everything is logical and well thought out.

It's clear the creators play-tested this game. On a solo run (playing as two players) and a multiplayer run of four players, the games were close. I just barely won the solo game, and we just barely lost the multiplayer game, when both were set on the "Novice" initial storm level.

RATING: 7.5
Forget Forbidden Island. This game buries it in a sandstorm of better mechanics, refined ideas, and brilliant design. I'm surprised how well this game works, and how ineffective Forbidden Island is in comparison.
GET THIS GAME!
Tense, action packed, and it doesn't suffer from the issue that plagues other cooperative games: it's not always obvious what is the "Next Right Thing To Do." It keeps you guessing, and prevents "bossy" types from dominating the choices of individual players.
The end game is a little fiddly.
I think they left out some essential "what about this?" questions that, as designers, they were blind too, but even then, it's still fun and you can house rule the ending anyway you want.

RATING: 6
It's bigger and more complex than "Forbidden Island", but that doesn't make it better (or worse). It's also much less visually appealing. The artwork on the tiles cannot be really appreciated, as they start face-down, showing only desert, and are often covered by sand tiles after revealed.

You are again doing a couple of simple actions and using your character's special power, trying to get some stuff and moving to a given location to escape. Clearing sand is analogous to draining water in its predecessor. Otherwise, however, the two games are not too similar. The "Pandemic" deck mechanic is gone and the pressure comes mainly from surviving with the scarce water. Also, in order to get the items you need to win, instead of collecting cards, you actually have to determine their location by searching for a pair of coordinates. The game is not something I need to own, but still a worthy addition to the series.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9

Kalandorok keresik az ősi városban az Elveszett Hajót jutalomként, azonban egy szörnyű viharnak hála a jutalom egyben az életben maradásuk feltétele is, mert csak a segítségével juthatnak ki a tikkasztó, veszedelmes sivatagból. Minden erőtöket összeszedve egy csapatként kell küzdeni a túlélésért (minden csepp vízért) kihasználva speciális képességeiteket és „plusz” feladatként – ha ennyi nem is lenne elég – meg kell találni az alkatrészeket, hogy a hajót összerakva „elvágtassatok” a naplementébe.

RATING: 7.5

RATING: 8
Game ina box 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
I was very luke warm on Forbidden Island. It is a great game for beginners and kids, but there is not much substance there compared to say Pandemic. This game, however, is superb. I love the fact that they have gone away from the set collection mechanic. To win this game on elite is quite a challenge with 3 characters. It requires you to really utilize each player's ability to its fullest. This is something that I also find with Pandemic on harder difficulty, while I can beat Forbidden Island on elite most of the time regardless of which character I have in play. 

There are two elements that can break you in this game - sand piles and lack of water. Playing with more people actually makes the game harder because you can die between turns easier by running out of water. As you play with more characters water management becomes very important. Sand management can be more difficult with fewer characters because you have less board coverage. This adds another layer of complexity and replay ability, especially solo as you vary the number of characters that you use. 

I would recommend this game to anyone who likes co-ops regardless of whether or not you like Forbidden Island. The games are substantially different. It is still simple enough to break out with kids and newbies, plays great solo, and can be brutally hard for your advanced gaming group.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Forbidden Desert takes us back to the coop world of Forbidden Island, as players try to reclaim 4 items, then escape a deathtrap, in this case a very lethal desert.

The neat thing is that Leacock has reimagined how his game punishes players again, by using the shifting sands to limit travel, and also to make getting to the target space more difficult by moving sands.

The player abilities are similar, but desert focused, and the items to be recovered are the pieces of a fabled flying ship that will (hopefully) take the players to safety.

This is as strong a game as Forbidden Island- possibly better- so on a 1st play of a favored designer, I'll jump to a 7.5.

Leacock hits another co-op out of the park.

RATING: 7
With much trepidation, I bought this game for my 7-year old.  He loves Forbidden Island, but I was worried that this one's mechanics were going to be a bit much for him.  I'm glad to say I was wrong; he picked it up just fine.  Now he loves this game as much as FI.  In fact, for his 8th birthday, he wants to play both games back-to-back.  I chuckled and said we didn't have to wait for his birthday, but I can make sure we pencil it in.

The game is similar to Forbidden Desert, but different enough that we enjoy playing both.  For us, it doesn't completely replace Forbidden Island, but I could see that it could for many people.

The shifting sandstorm mechanic is great.  The threat of the sun is very real, too, and definitely adds a lot of tension to the game.  Hide in the tunnels too much to avoid the sun and the sand starts to pile up.  We've definitely lost before because we ran out of sand tiles.

This game is another hit from Matt Leacock; I can't wait to see what he does next.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Cooperative game in which you're all trying to escape from a desert in which the sands are rapidly rising, and you're all at risk of succumbing to the scorching sun.

Very similar to its predecessor Forbidden Island, and that's perhaps why I have given it not such a high score (although I enjoy this game thoroughly).  I just don't think there's room for both games in anyone's collection, they're too similar and both are played in the same sort of way.

The other reason I have not scored this particularly highly is that it's a little too formulaic.  By this I mean that you will basically be on auto-pilot after a few plays, and there isn't a huge range of googlies that the game can throw your way.  I believe Pandemic is better at that, and I prefer the card mechanic in that game to this one.

All that said, this is a strong game - it encourages discourse with your fellow players, it can often be tense (especially towards the end), and it is simple to teach.  Recommended for families and for playing with non-gamer pals.

RATING: 10
This is one of the absolute best Cooperative-Set Collection games out there. It's very intense as you try to collect your items and escape from the sinking island. Many of plays of this game result in shouting and wringing of hands followed by cheering when we've snatched victory from the soggy hands of death. It's simple enough to be considered a kids game, but deep enough to be enjoyed by adults. This is not just a "younger" version of Pandemic. It's similar, but more intense co-op game with amazing art and fantastic components.

RATING: 7.5
One of the best puzzle style game I played along with Pandemic. But unlike Pandemic, this one had much stronger theme - with each sand storm moving about, it gave very desperate feeling of being buried alive in the desert, and dying of thirst compared to move around clearing cubes off the board while discarding 5 same colored cards to find cure. 

The game is not easy by any means - it seems a bit luck dependent with what storm card gets flipped. But the randomness is welcoming challenge in this one. Very nice co-operative game that definitely deserves a praise. I can easily recommend this game out to everyone.

Parted to my good friend's birthday present. Hope they won't find it too hard to beat it!

RATING: N/A
[b][url=https://boardgamegeek.com/wiki/page/BoardGameGeek_Golden_Geek#toc2]2013 Golden Geek Winner[/url][/b]

In Forbidden Desert, a thematic sequel to Forbidden Island, players take on the roles of brave adventurers who must throw caution to the wind and survive both blistering heat and blustering sand in order to recover a legendary flying machine buried under an ancient desert city. While featuring cooperative gameplay similar to Forbidden Island, Forbidden Desert is a fresh new game based around an innovative set of mechanisms, such as an ever-shifting board, individual resource management, and a unique method for locating the flying machine parts.

Players: 2, 3, 4, 5
Time: 45 min
Mechanics: [property=2001][/property], [property=2023][/property], [property=2676][/property], [property=2011][/property], [property=2004][/property], [property=2015][/property]

RATING: 8
- 2-5 player
- Weight: Medium (easy to grasp, hard to win)
- Genre: Cooperative
- Length: Medium 

I (Keith) really like co-op games and this is one of my favorites. The components are high quality, the art design is great, and the gameplay is fun. Despite being made by the same game designer as Pandemic this game feels different and new. Don't expect an easy win when playing this game, especially when playing with 4-5 people. We have lost far more than we have won. It's not so hard that you feel cheated however, as every loss has been very close and every win has felt very satisfying like you really overcame a challenge together.

RATING: 8
Slightly simpler than Pandemic, but as unforgiving for new players. Engrossing game, fun to introduce and play with non-gamers and gamers alike. Despite its simplicity complex strategies can arise, especially towards  the less forgiving higher difficulty levels.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A challenging game with superb artworks and well balanced characters. One of the good sized games you can play with anyone and it's nice that each game is fairly short. The concept of an ever-changing board is awesome, but it doesn't work out all that well since the sand mainly builds up in the edges (especially on turned tiles) and the storm often gets stuck in corners. It also lacks some strategy, since you barely need a idea of where you're moving. I think the equips could have been more powerful and unique by replacing a few equipment tiles with bedrock. One of the downsides with it being a co-op game is that the most experienced players often decide what to do. All in all, 10 for being the best co-op game I've played, but only 7 for the game overall.

RATING: N/A
In Forbidden Desert, a thematic sequel to Forbidden Island, players take on the roles of brave adventurers who must throw caution to the wind and survive both blistering heat and blustering sand in order to recover a legendary flying machine buried under an ancient desert city. While featuring cooperative gameplay similar to Forbidden Island, Forbidden Desert is a fresh new game based around an innovative set of mechanisms, such as an ever-shifting board, individual resource management, and a unique method for locating the flying machine parts.

RATING: 9
I rate games high, and I rate them high because I rate them  according to niche. For instance as a light family move and find, i.e. "action point allowance", this game shines. I enjoy the mechanics and I enjoy the co-op, and the pretty tiles and I enjoy the moving tiles and the character abilities and how everything just makes sense. I didn't care for losing tiles in Forbidden Island (although I never played, just watched it played) and Forbidden Island just BURIES tiles, but with a dune blaster card it's easy to get your card back. My only gripe, and one that should drop the rating down is how cheap the construction is. My cards at play through three look like they took a beating from many game nights. Likewise the tiles are already chipping on the sides. This might not seem so bad but the goal is tile secrecy - you don't necessarily WANT to know what's under a tile because it's supposed to be a surprise. That being said the price was good, i like the tin box, everything fits well, the ship is fun and overall it was a good value. I looked forward to it and I was not disappointed - except for the wear, that was sad.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The 2nd cooperative board game I've obtained (the first being Pandemic).  I decided to buy this game after watching the episode of Wil Wheaton's YouTube series 'Tabletop' that it featured in and I have not been disappointed.  Players have to work together to search the titular desert for the four critical pieces to a legendary flying machine in order to escape before they either die of thirst, are buried alive by sand, or swept away by a quickly intensifying sand storm. 

For a hobby that can get quite expensive, Forbidden Desert provides a nearly unbeatable return on investment due to it's low price point (currently $19.99 on Amazon). And by no means does that mean that the quality of the components suffer - far from it.  The game comes in a sturdy metal tin (that's right a tin), features quality cards and thick game pieces.  The game art is gorgeous and features a fun, steam-punk theme to it.  The rules are straightforward and easy to explain and the core rules fit on the back of a playing card for easy player reference - plus being a cooperative game there are no barriers to experienced players helping new players along.  There's a ton of replay value as the board is different each time, and like Pandemic there are several different roles for players to choose from that each confer their own special advantage and the difficulty level can be set from Novice to Expert. And the game itself is no slouch - even on the novice setting it's a struggle until the bitter end.

I honestly don't know why this game isn't as popular as Pandemic - although I suspect what gives Pandemic the edge is the theme - admittedly saving the world from global deadly diseases is a bit more appealing than trying to assemble an anachronistic flying ship before choking on sand.  I'd actually argue that Forbidden Desert is more challenging than Pandemic given the variable board game that rearranges itself after each turn and that spaces can become inaccessible if buried by sand (as opposed to Pandemic where the board is static and you always have the same freedom of movement throughout the game).

Regardless, if you like cooperative games - Forbidden Desert will be an excellent addition to your game collection/closet/Rubbermaid tub - and at it's low price it's an easy pickup.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This game is basically a re-fiddle of Forbidden Island and for that reason I'll keep the rating to an 8.  While it definitely adds some complexity to the game, it still feels pretty familiar.  Also, the beautiful tension that FI provides through its mechanic of the island sinking around the adventurers is not as palpable in the Desert version.  That said, the game is still an enormous amount of fun, and is an absolutely fantastic introduction to co-op games. 

UPDATE:  5 games in and the thing keeps getting better and better.  There is a NOTICEABLE jump in difficulty even between Novice and Normal, which adds considerably to that "tension" that I missed from FI, and the Meteorologist role is a great idea with a GREAT ability that can come back to bite you later on in the game.  Upping my rating to a 9.

RATING: 7
Rating based on solo play only.

This is a game in the same vein as Pandemic (using limited action points to control a spreading danger while working toward a win goal), but simpler, faster, and with more luck elements. The moving storm mechanic is very clever, and I really like the feeling of piling more and more sand on.

For my solo-ing tastes, it feels a little too out of control as there are many unpredictable elements... however this is also the same aspect that I think would make this a good co-op to actually play with other people! Unlike Pandemic, in which the logistics can be complicated to the point where I don't see how you could win without hands being open information and someone taking charge, FD is more straightforward and action-y, where each person can make their own decisions and yet they are still *good* decisions (which isn't to say it's an easy game to win; it's not). This would likely be the game I would use to introduce co-ops.

------------------------------------------------

Gave to my sis-in-law, who I think would really like this, plus I generally only want to play co-ops with family anyway (Pandemic would be my solo choice for this type of game).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
Decent coop game, but after multiple plays it lost its lustre far quicker than pandemic. I think this is because it is much more simplistic/repetitive:
1) Geography is straightforward, and
2) One type of resource (e.g. versus various types of diseases and trading off what to keep/discard in hand)
Thus every game feels too similar/using same process.

The difficulty gradient also seems off: I have no losses on the easiest 2 levels, and no wins on the highest difficulty level. When I lose at hardest, feels more luck-based / impossible than something I can get better at.

Maybe better for teaching people new to the hobby, but other than that I'm thinking not really worth owning if you have pandemic (too similar, but more simplistic).

RATING: 8
Another great cooperative game by Matt Leacock.  The obvious comparisons here are Forbidden Island and Pandemic, and I would generally agree with the popular opinion that this falls between those two in terms of complexity and depth.  The art is lackluster, which is a bit disappointing since Forbidden Island is gorgeous.  The ship components are cool, but they don't really add much to the game (kids like them).  I do enjoy that this offers a more compelling, challenging game than Forbidden Island and is something I would definitely bring out with a group of adults, although it's still on the "light" side for gamers.  The co-op feel works very well in that players really need to coordinate plans in advance, although the game does an excellent job of regularly throwing a wrench in the works.  The sand movement between turns is really cool and provides a great level of challenge without feeling punishing.  I did have one minor component issue in that all of my X-shaped sand tiles are bowed a bit -- this may have just been a fairly isolated issue and it really doesn't cause any problems during play.  At the price, this is one I would quickly recommend for families, although I wish I could combine the gameplay from this with the art from Forbidden Island.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[microbadge=1714]

[u]09/06/2013[/u]:  I feel Forbidden Desert falls very nicely in between its two older cousins - Pandemic and Forbidden Island.  It adds more complexity than Forbidden Island but not nearly as much as Pandemic with its expansion.  There are more decisions to be made than with FI but (again) not as many as Pandemic.

In FD, you are a group of Adventurers who crash landed on an ancient city buried under sand.  You need to find the four machine parts to the mystical flying machine and escape the ever growing sand dunes and blazing sun.

There are tiles and and a deck of cards similar to FI, but the mechanisms are definitely different.  Here the tiles move and sand is added to the tiles creating a barrier for movement and excavating.  Ignore the increasing dunes of sand and become buried forever.  The Sun beats down on the Adventurers causing them to use their varying supplies of precious water.  Drink too much, depleting your canteens, and dehydration consumes them.

This is a very well done followup to FI.  I feel both games can easily be part of the same game collection.  FI is for those times when you want something a little more casual or have a lighter game group at the table.  If they want more of a challenge, then head on over to FD.  And for those wanting more variety and a deeper group puzzle, there's Pandemic.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
Unlike its weaker cousin [gameid=65244], Forbidden Desert presents quite the cooperative challenge in a unique experience. This time rather than waiting around for the right cards, you're up against the clock bigtime. The ruins are filling up with sand, you're running out of water and the storms are getting stronger.

Players really need to work together utilizing their special skills and items in smart ways. Like its cousin the components are top-notch. I appreciate what Leacock came up with to make the sandstorm move around the board, causing havoc.

RATING: 6.5
After 1 play, it's similar to Forbidden Island (obviously) but has a few important differences:

- Trading something doesn't cost an action.
- No cards to collect and discard.
- Rather than simply moving to a tile and getting the goodie there, you must find 2 "clues" for each goodie, then it is located at the intersection of those 2 clue tiles.

RATING: 5
Forbidden Desert is surprisingly fiddly for such a small game: moving around the tiles and stacking the sand tiles atop them gets really tedious (especially since they you need to flip & rearrange them way too often).  More importantly, mostly what you're doing is moving around & blindly peeking under desert tiles.  There is no real strategy or tactics to that:  shall I blindly look under here or there?  How do I know?  When you loose, the most you can say is: "too bad we hadn't blindly looked under the right tiles sooner."

RATING: 8
A híresztelések igazak, sajnos sok a hibás alkatrész, amik a játékra is kihatnak.. :( Megjelölt/hibás lapkák és lapok.. A kiadó pedig kérés után szintén rosszat küldött.. + a mostani első játéknál vettem észre 2 viharkártyán, hogy hibás.. Hát nem egyszerű..
Na de maga a játék? Nekem német nyelvű van meg (Bécsben vettem 15 Euróért), 3-an próbáltuk ki, a többiek segítettek nekem a nyelvi kérdésekben (karakterkártyák és felszereléskártyák). A figurák miatt ezt tartom jobbnak! :)
Első játékban kikaptunk mint a huzat (azt hiszem pont én haltam szomjan.. :P ) A másodikat viszont éppen hogy megnyertük. Mind a kétszer a legkönnyebb fokozaton játszottunk, 3an, véletlenszerű karakterválasztással.
A játék látványa (a felsorolt KOMOLY hibáktól eltekintve) gyönyörű, a játékélmény kiváló! Számunkra visszaadta a hangulatot teljes mértékben! A két leányzó akikkel nekivágtam, oda-vissza van a játéktól, végig agyalós, kicsit kockáztatós, utolsó pillanatig izgalmas játék. Végén persze lehet pacsizni, de nem rajtunk múlik teljes mértékben a siker, kell jó adag szerencse is (viharlapok, mit mikor találunk meg). Ezért sikerélményben számomra elmarad a Hanabitól, ahol egy jól lerakott lap már felér egy végső győzelemmel, így játék során többször átélem azt az emóciót, mint a Die Vergessene Stadt-nál.
De szombaton újra nyomjuk! :)

RATING: 7.5
Superior to Forbidden Island, with that much needed "something" added to it. Looks pretty and I really like the way the storm moves around and changes the board, even though drawing loads of cards at the end of each player's turn & moving the storm around is a bit cumbersome, especially when the storm count is high. But it really adds a cool tactile feel to the game. At its best Forbidden Desert really is a cool and exciting rollercoaster ride from "we're ok!" to "oh no we're totally not!"

I'm not sure whether the game has legs for dozens of plays, but after a few plays it feels like an excellent option for a lighter co-op & with the scaling difficulty level you can make it insanely hard. Also good for a solo game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
An interesting follow up game to Forbidden Island, that fortunately adds a 5th player! I found the mechanics to be improved in most ways over Forbidden Island, though I still enjoy that game as well.  Not having to carry a hand of cards that force you to collect and trade just to get a winning artifact, not unlike Pandemic, was a refreshing change to a co-op game.  It also felt a little more team based, as all players had to worry about each others water levels as they their turns passed by.  The concept of finding where two clue tiles line up to find the location of a hidden item was interesting, and not having to shuffle cards back into the desk constantly was also nice.  The only mechanic that felt a tad "fidley" was the storm.  Each time someone finishes their turn, you must draw from the storm desk and more the tiles on the board as the storm moves, while also placing sand tiles as the storm moves across the board.  It's a nice mechanic, but I think it felt a little fiddly, and some what hindered my groups desire to play a 3rd time in a row.  By no means a big deal, and certainly a fun mechanic.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.6
Really fun. For how simple and euro style it is, it really has a strong theme of feeling like your stuck in the desert, trying to get the parts you need to escape before either the sandstorm takes you or you die of thrist. There's a fast paced and sense of urgency to it and it's easy to learn and play without being so simple that it just feels like a children's game. I feel like there's probably more strategy in this game then I realized since we did 2 player novice and barely escaped. I don't think I used jetpacks correctly. I like the player powers and how they make sense. Doing the sandstorm activity in between turns does break up the game and slow it down a bit. Many cooperative games I like have "bad guy" phases that seem to take up too much of the game so I can't complain too much. It fits a good niche that for me, replaces pandemic which is slightly heavier--of having a nice, easy to teach, fairly thematic, fully cooperative game that takes less than an hour and people can enjoy it the first time. I'm sure pandemic is great and I still want to play, but for my collection and my needs/tastes, this one is my light fully coop game where we each play a different character in a fairly euro style.

RATING: 6.5
--- Preliminary thoughts ---

It takes Forbidden Island (tiles, 4 actions, race vs clock, etc) and modifies it to add more complexity and place it further from Pandemic: adds exploration, the board moves, cards to sink tiles not needed anymore, etc.

It's not only more complex, but also more difficult to win and more thematic (refloating islands never convinced me).

It's the game that Forbidden Island would have had to be.

I still dislike the tin box though.

RATING: 6
[b]Forbidden Desert[/b] was traded away in a math trade 2/10/16. (Received Survive: Escape from Atlantis + the 5&6 player expansion.)

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (6):[/COLOR]

[i]Yet another co-op that didn't survive in our collection. After playing it a bunch when we first got it, we soon stopped playing. Part of the reason was the difficulty spike compared to Forbidden Island, Forbidden Desert is much less forgiving and more demanding due to not only finding the treasure but also having to manage water for each character. My youngest daughter has been playing Forbidden Island with us since it is simpler and more straight forward so I wasn't sad to see Forbidden Desert go. Honestly I'd still rather play Forbidden Island, I prefer the game mechanics, art and variable tile set up.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- Another fun, family co-op designed by Matt Leacock (Forbidden Island/Pandemic) with typical top notch art and components. 
- Happy to find out that it plays much differently than Forbidden Island and is a definite step up in difficulty (this game can be brutal). 
- The sand building up on the board is really helps immerse you in the theme and helps build tension. 
- A few role repeats and some brand new ones; what's cool is the old roles still feel fresh because of how differently this game plays out and the interactions with the new roles. 
- I enjoy having to find the pieces by uncovering the two tiles and finding where they intersect to unearth the treasure. 
- Quick playtime, Forbidden Desert is another game we can easily bust out on a night when we don't have a lot of time to play a game. It also helps that it's a co-op so there won't be hurt feelings when playing with tired kids who are begging me to play a game.[/i]

RATING: 7.5
A perfect sequel to Forbidden Island! This game is cooperative like FI, but the mechanics are fresh and new enough to really enjoy owning and playing both games. If you like the original, I just can't see you not liking this one. The sand really make this game tough to win and sure look great for the theme. 

I am impressed with the clever design and look to this game. The box storage is also excellent. I'm not a fan of metal tins but at least there is room for everything. Since I sleeve my cards, I store them under the plastic insert. 

There also is a vertical board that indicates the current danger level to the game and an air ship that you build to escape the desert. When you have collected the parts to the ship and make your way to the landing sight, you build your ship and fly away.

RATING: 7
規則:
*版塊蓋著洗勻牌成5x5中間留一格，照菱形的形狀擺放8個沙漠標記到板塊上(淡色面朝上)，組裝沙暴標記然後根據人數跟難度放標記，風暴卡跟裝備卡洗勻蓋著放置一旁，飛船裝備也拆好放一旁
*探險者卡洗勻一人發一張，然後標記你的水量到最大值，拿一個對應米寶放在起始飛機墜毀版塊，隨機起始
*每次行動分成兩個階段直到勝利或失敗
1.花費最多四個行動點來做行動
>移動 一格到相鄰版塊，背面的沙漠標記不能過去，沒版塊也不行
>移除沙 可移除一個沙標記在你所在地或相鄰版塊
>挖掘 將沒有沙的版塊翻面並處理效果
>拾取 拿起1個零件在已經翻面的版塊，放在面前
*當四個零件收集到，集合到起飛點就獲勝
*免費行動 同版塊時可分享水跟傳遞裝備卡
**版塊效果**
>水 左下有水標記的翻面可能會有井，此時上面所有玩家獲得兩個水
>齒輪 抽一張裝備卡，可隨時使用
>零件 翻到兩張同零件時座標交會點為零件所在地，兩張都開就把零件放在交會點
>隧道 可移動到另外一個隧道(兩個以上沙不能到隧道板塊上)，且在上面的玩家不用在太陽卡出現時喝水
>起飛版 要贏的集合點
2.根據沙暴表的數值抽對應張數沙暴卡，一張一張結算
>移動 根據圖示移動對應版塊到空格區，並把移動的版塊上面放置一個沙(兩個以上的沙不能通過，可翻面表示)，如果你的版塊上面有兩個沙則要先花行動移除到一個以下才能做其他動作，卡牌抽完就洗勻在抽
*當沙不夠放時直接輸掉遊戲
>提升沙暴標記 提升標記一格，如果到最上面則直接輸掉
>太陽 沒在隧道的喝一個水，如果到骷顱符號則死亡，輸掉遊戲

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Sure it's a spin off and a variation on a theme, but it definitely feels like an improvement over Forbidden Island. For starters, it changes a simple hold-back-time race game into an exploration race game, where you must go out and find things in order to win. You can let go tiles you've already explored to the sand storm, but if things are building up on unexplored tiles, you could be in trouble as you'll have to spend actions digging things out. Luckily there's a few gear cards you can find that will save you from disaster. That is until the water for each player starts running out, which is a second type of disaster card in the deck. The water requirement forces more co-operation and discussion in order to get people together at the oasis to recover enough to keep going for long enough. Just that one extra dimension improves the co-operation aspect significantly. An enjoyable thumbs up.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
"Excellent thematic co-op. Straightforward rules, but has interesting decisions. My wife and I like it a lot better than Pandemic or Forbidden Island."

What I like:
- Pure co-op; good theme; great components (and inexpensive)
- I love that there is no abstract set collection element
- Really clever storm/sand mechanisms
- More opportunities for cooperation than Forbidden Island

What I don't like:
- Can run a bit long with 4-5p (75+ minutes)
- Not a fan of tin boxes, especially a different size than Forbidden Island

While sharing some aspects with Forbidden Island, this is a pretty clear improvement. It is more thematic, requires more cooperation, probably has more tough decisions, and feels a bit less random.

I would put the weight around 1.9, slightly higher than BGG voters.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Forbidden Desert is a purely cooperative game roughly based on the system used in the designer's previous games, Pandemic and Forbidden Island. Here, players take on various rule-breaking roles to explore a desert tile board, trying to find various airship parts plus the landing pad to escape. A sandstorm moves around the board as determined by randomly drawn cards, burying tiles it touches in sand, making tiles unable to be explored or even crossed until unburied. If a tile has no sand, it can be explored, revealing one of two clues that will reveal the location of one of four airship parts (think latitude and longitude), the landing pad, a tunnel that can be used to traverse to other tunnels and hide from the sun, an oasis that can refill water, or a blank tile that provides the explorer with a random bonus card. Mixed in with the cards that move the sandstorm around are cards that make adventurers lose water and cards that increase the number of sandstorm cards drawn. Players must find all four parts and get to the landing pad before any of them runs out of water. While this is still a family-weight game, it's more complex than something like Forbidden Island and I enjoyed it more because of that. However, it's still a cooperative game that's largely depending on luck, which isn't really my cup of tea.

(1 play)

RATING: 6
The game is fun, but there are some serious balancing issues. There is nothing preventing you from just failing because the "Sun beats down" on you it the first 12 cards or so. 
If you don't find caves or if you fall on the mirage you may also, through no fault of your own, lose the game. I would say that the Meteorologists power loses strength the more player you have, so he is better in a 2 player game. Also I'm under the impression the for a 3+ player game the game is balanced taking the Navigators talent into account. I think that the Navigator+Climber combo is so powerful that the game kind of assume they will be part of the group.

So it is light, it is generally fun, I mainly play it with my kids. Strategy-wise, I'd say there are many ways you can lose where you couldn't have done much depending on how the storm evolves and whether or not you find the right locations or items.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
So Forbidden Desert is the revamp/sequel to Forbidden Island. Both of these were the groundwork from which the overly ubiquitous Co-op hobby game Pandemic, from which a whole franchise has arisen. Compared to Forbidden Desert, Island shouldn't even exist, and Pandemic clearly has some common ground. Designer Matt Leacock clearly knows how to build co-op games with player roles and building threats, but if you've played one of his games, you're not going to find much richness or diversity in his collection of designs (including the upcoming Thunderbirds game).

Your goal in this game is to gather various parts of your airship (the steampunk element in this games aesthetics surprised me and frankly pissed me off; why does an airship need a GIANT SUNDIAL on it's bow?) before the desert storm (not the US/Iran conflict of the 80's) consumes you. You get four actions a turn (Which will sound familiar to the Pandemic players) to clean up sand (outbreaks) and flip over tiles to find clues to your ship parts. Then storm cards flip and affect you, most notably adding sand to the tiles, and/or draining your limited water reserves. The game ends if you get overwhelmed with sand, or you run out of water.

RATING: 7.499
Similar to Forbidden Island, but better.  The 4 components needed to win are found by excavating tiles that give the column and the row (rather than by set collection like Pandemic and Forbidden Island).

There are several ways to lose.  You can get buried in sand (run out of sand tiles because you let them build up).  You can die of thirst (not going to the wells/tunnels enough).  You can die if you aren't quick enough and the sand storm spins out of control.

Good game.  fun.  the components of the little ship are fun....the kids love to handle them like Forbidden Island.

Good game.  Definitely an improvement.

Our favorite co-op is still Flash Point:  Fire Rescue.  We prefer the theme...and seems a little more 'exciting' with life and death of innocent victims hanging in the balance. 

Video review:  http://www.boardgamegeek.com/video/40410/forbidden-desert/dice-tower-reviews-forbidden-island-the-charters

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is the latest game from the designer of Pandemic and Forbidden Island. It is a co-operative game for two or more players, a pure co-op with no traitor and as with his other games open communication. This falls somewhere between the other two games, it is not as strategic as Pandemic but it jettisons less of that games complexity than Forbidden Island so it is a little less child friendly.
Players turn over tiles, which the game is regularly covering in sand, in order to find 4 pieces of a ship in order to escape the desert. They do this without getting buried by the sand, running out of time, or exhausting their supply of water.
Its clever and the theme appeals more to other players I know than Pandemic so will see some table time. Fortunately the rules are easy to understand (unlike some recent co-op card games) so everyone can follow what is happening and contribute to the discussion of what strategy should be followed.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
This is the game that got me back into hobby board games after quite a long hiatus (Settlers of Catan in the late 90's, Evo and Puerto Rico in the early 2000's).

Unlike the games listed above, this game has an overall different feel (it is a cooperative game).  Many people say that Pandemic is a superior game (it is definitely more popular), but I find Forbidden Desert to be more elegant in its design, gameplay, and artwork.  I love the theme and the mystery and perpetual puzzle of trying to unearth the buried city and escape before time runs out!  It's a really great game and will no doubt be in my collection for the rest of my gaming career!

RATING: 4.9
Played with an 8 year old and an 11 year old, this game is just about right.  The rules are easy enough for them to pick up, and they don't get swamped with decisions.

Sadly, this indicates that there isn't much depth or strategy to it.  The wind doth blow, and you make the best of the situation, rinse (in sand) and repeat until victory or death.

I have to ding this compared to Forbidden Island because it lacks that marvellous mechanic of urgent hazard on a Waters Rise restack.  In Desert, the sand just piles up monotonously until either you dune blast it or parch.

Randomly digging around is fun a couple of times, but adults might like to look elsewhere. I won't say the P- word, but you're all thinking it.

RATING: 6
A good improvement on Forbidden Desert, although it's actually quite different (Forbidden Island feeling very much just like a simpler version of Pandemic).  There's a lot less randomness from the luck of the draw like in the other games - sand is going to pile up and the some tiles are going to get moved each round - and it's much more about managing your actions, the amount of sand on the board, and the amount of water everyone has, with none of the set collection that most other co-ops seem to center around.  It's more like a spatial puzzle to solve, but the pieces of the puzzle are moving around.  Seems probably best with 2 or 3.

This means though that I have to rein in what could be the best options on my own volition, just to make sure other players are making their own choices. This is not really a problem but ultimately, I probably prefer it if a game naturally compartmentalizes people's roles.

RATING: 5
More of the same... Although this game *feels* different than Forbidden Island and isn't just another Pandemic Lite, the mechanisms really aren't all that different.  Sinking tiles versus moving tiles getting buried isn't really *that* different; getting a special action card from certain tiles isn't that different from possibly getting one in a random draw.  Whatever.... Overall, Forbidden Dessert adds onto what was in Forbidden Island and is definitely more difficult, but it's not really better, worse, or more or less fun. It's just okay and not something that I need to own.  Maybe I'm just becomes less and less a fan of cooperative games, although I do REALLY like Freedom: The Underground Railroad quite a bit (probably because it's a lot more "Euro" in design and is unlike any other game I've played before).  Forbidden Island is just an unnecessary sequel.  Nice bits at a pretty good price though, but that's not enough to add it to my collection.
