RATING: 8
I really enjoy playing this game. The board games I'm able to play regularly need to be restricted in complexity and length. Forbidden Desert does well in both categories. It's also a cooperative game, which is a new and appealing concept to new players. The groups I play this with certainly don't always make optimal choices, and this game is more often than not a nail-biter until the very end.

The storm shifting the playing area is a welcome addition to the static board of Forbidden Island. I like Forbidden Desert more than Forbidden Island. The latter seemed easier to "figure out." The great theme and replay value make Forbidden Desert a keeper.

RATING: 3
Seems less transparent and simple than Forbidden Island (which is a baby's game), but I think it's more boring. Also more complicated. Maybe I was jaded by this series of reskinned games by the time I played it but the payoff just doesn't seem to be there. Nor does the tension -- the threats aren't as clear and definitive, and there's no equivalent of "reshuffle discard and put on top of deck" mechanic to give an increasing sense of danger. Just walk around digging shit up, hoping you find what you need before you randomly die of thirst or get buried under sand at unpredictable intervals. That's not to say that tactics aren't important, but the suspense wasn't there. 

Also, the maintenance steps in this are kinda tedious. Pandemic > Forbidden Island > Forbidden Desert.

Unless I was taught wrong, which is possible, but seemed legit.

[b]I'd Rather Play:[/b] Pandemic

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
First of all I have to dispute the pretty common claim that this game is very different from Forbidden Island...it's not at all.  It is really just the same game with a couple of updates.

In this game you're in a desert made up of tiles.  The action system is the same, you get 4 actions each turn and use them to move, exchange items, and clear and excavate tiles.  Instead of a tide there is a sand storm and instead of sinking tiles they are covered with sand.  There are special items that do pretty much the same things (jet pack instead of helicopter and dune blaster instead of sandbags).  And instead of finding sets of treasures you are finding the 4 missing pieces of your crashed helicopter before returning to the exit tile and leaving on a helicopter.

See, it's the same damn game.  And as such it faces the same problem as Forbidden Island...it's not as good as many other coop games.  Especially Pandemic which is just an all around direct replacement.

I did rate this a little higher than Forbidden Island because of some of the kind of neat mechanics that are added to this game.  The pushing around of the tiles and ever changing map is kind of neat and I like the oasis/mirage mechanic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The little brother of "Forbidden Island" is its big brother! With FI I was always a disappointed by how easy it was to win, this one seems harder. It has the same family friendly appeal, it is easily playable in half an hour (unlike many co-ops), it comes with similar mechanics but there is more going on. Besides retrieving the 4 objectives, the group has to make sure no player is running out of water, which gives a new edge. There is just more one has to do in "Forbidden Desert". I know in FI I often did not use all of my possible actions, here you will need them all. 
Thematically it seems stronger, too, finding and digging parts of the airship out of the sand of the desert you crashed in seems something more likely to risk my life for than 4 random treasures. 
I wish this had come out first, we own FI and it is not different enough to justify its way into our collection but I think I would choose FD over FI.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Family co-op game from Matt Leacock (Pandemic). Players move pawns around a semi-randomized grid of face-down tiles, looking for the airship components they can use to escape. A cruel event deck moves tiles, distributes sand (which needs to be dug out) or makes the sun beat down until they die of thirst, but tiles not directly pointing to an exit space usually provide useful items.

Mechanically and thematically it works well but the luck factor is significant, especially on higher difficulty levels. Navigator + climber seems overpowered.

Solid family game but too light to be of interest as a puzzle.

You really can't ask for much more out of a pure Co-Op game. My nitpicks would be that I have lost this game the first round before it got back to my turn in a 3 player game once. Alpha players and/or players who want decisions made for them can somewhat dampen the experience but that is not the games fault necessarily.

RATING: 7
I like the moving tiles and the sand aspect of this game, and also having to share water. It is not easy to win even at novice level. Having played it a few times, I realize that it still suffers from quarterbacking, but definitely less so than Pandemic because there are so many aspects to balance. No one decision is a 100% perfect decision, so more constructive discussion takes place. Try not to end a game session with this game because it is quite tense and could leave a bitter taste if there is no win. Best to follow up with a competitive game so everyone has the satisfaction of pitting against each other and earning some credit instead of leaving the session having lost to a cooperative game.

RATING: 9
Go ahead and sell Forbidden Island. Or give it away. Either way, you won't need to play it ever again after getting Forbidden Desert. FD replaces FI in every possible way: it's more thematic, it adds an element of exploration, and it's way more fun. It also gets rid of the clunky card mechanics of trying to hand cards back and forth until you have the right ones. This game is all about trying to discover the right tiles, then getting out of town before you succumb to the desert heat. This is the best entry-level co-op game out there.

RATING: 6
After playing Forbidden Island and Pandemic a few times, I feel like I am almost always able to assess the best actions to perform. Feels like only an unlucky shuffle of cards will lose the game.
Forbidden Desert does not feel the same way. Along with the luck involved in shuffling the cards, you are forced to make tough decisions due to necessary information being hidden under the tiles. 
The game is more difficult to win as the best choices are not as obvious. Because of this, Forbidden Desert has provided the best cooperative experience of the Leacock co-ops I've played.

RATING: 7.5
Gotta give Matt Leacock credit, the man knows how to design good co-ops. I like this one, while similar to Pandemic, I feel like the tension is higher for the whole game, and then ramps up near the end. There are a few ways to lose the game (buried alive, run out of water, the storm intensity gets too high) so it seems to add to the tension. Also, with all of the different concerns the optimal move is not always evident, which cuts down on Alpha-gaming. I like it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
PROS: Fun coop game, easy to learn and highly enjoyable in it's gameplay and theme. The graphics are attractive and the game works fine as a gateway for non-gamers. Different characters, difficulty levels and tile randomness add great replay value and different challenges. It's a good game from 2 to several players.

CONS: Somewhat luck dependant - The oasis' placement (may be too close to each other, you may find the mirage when you need water the most), the tiles you choose to explore (you may find easily the directions for pieces or not, and the pieces may be close to you or across the board, buried under 6 tiles of sand), the tunnels' locations (they may be too close to each other, which is bad), the way the storm's eye moves (it can get trapped in a corner doing nothing or hastefully cross the map depleting the sand tile pool), the equipment you draw, how many and when the suns and storms are drawn. On the latter, I haven't played a single match without at least one moment of "alright, if we get really unlucky now, we lose" when drawing storm cards. This unpredictability makes the tactical decisions limited to a certain extent (except when you are playing with certain characters), and you are not only playing against the game but also against probability and mischance; The clunky metal box is awful and its contents could easily fit a box half of its size. The desert tiles should be square cards - allowing sleeving - because they wear out and you end up with marked tiles. Also, I received 2 or 3 tiles with small print errors (dots) which are enough to distinguish these locations if someone tries a little harder to cheat.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Forbidden Desert is essentially Forbidden Island rethemed and improved.  Instead of sinking, land gets sand tokens piled on them.  The storm randomly moves around shifting tiles every which way and piling up more sand.  You have to dig out the sand to flip over tiles so that you can find the treasures, which in this game are parts of your crashed ship.  

Ship parts are located on the map according to where the two corresponding part tiles intersect.  Instead of water rising, this game has the sun beating down, which meakes you thirsty.  This is a desert where the sun only occasionally beats down... the best kind of desert to crash land in.  Opportunities to get water are very limited in the game and usually require everyone to be on the same square, which messes around with the go out and search part of the game.  

Once you find all the ship parts you have to find the launchpad and get everyone back there.  Luckily all deserts come with a buried launchpad, another little known fact about deserts.  

Now that I've played Forbidden Desert, I really would rather play it over Forbidden Island every time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
[floatright][ImageID=1528722][/floatright][thing=136063][/thing] has several similarities with his "middle brother" - [thing=65244][/thing], particularly regarding the abilities of the roles. The game dynamics is as follows: it is a cooperative game in which the players want to recover and rebuild a flying machine buried in the desert - this being the forbidden one, so you know it won't be an easy task. The machine was left in pieces and is necessary to explore the parts of the city in order to find them. All the while the desert itself is trying to murder the characters, beating them down with the inclement sun. Also the dunes shift in the wind, so things seem to move around.

The board is composed by 24 tiles in a grid of 5 x 5 with a space in the center. In each turn the player has four actions points to spend, and they can be used by moving (one point per tile), digging (one point per sand marker), exploring a tile (one point) and collecting the pieces of the of the machine (one point per piece). Players cannot move into tiles with two or more sand markers, being necessary to remove the sand first. Also is not allowed to explore a tile with sand markers on it. At the end of every player turn cards are revealed accordingly to the number on the sandstorm meter. The cards in this deck are in one of three types: sandstorm (rises the sandstorm level), suns beats down (drops the water level of the players) and directions cards that indicates how many and in what direction the tiles will move - each tile that moved receives a sand marker, and if a tile moves more than once, it receives a sand marker for each movement.

Players lose if the sand markers are depleted or if the character dies of thirsty (the level of water reaches the death level). And victory is achieved if all the pieces of the machine are collected and are taken to the hangar were they will be assembled - for this the tile must be clear of sand.

The game has more to it - special cards, tunnels, wells - but this is the basic.

[thing=136063][/thing], as [thing=65244][/thing], has a really high replay value and also shares the great pieces. One thing that [thing=136063][/thing] has an advantage is the use of actions: many times in [thing=65244][/thing] I found myself, or others, with nothing to do with the actions available. In [thing=136063][/thing] all the actions always counted for something. However without the Meteorologist, [thing=136063][/thing] seems to be more chaotic and unpredictable, so making strategies are harder to be put in place - this, by the way, has one positive point: since the it is harder to see a path, it is also harder for an alpha player to dominate, mainly because the lack, in some moments, of a clear "better move".

Anyway, the game hit strong notes with me, and I liked it quite a bit, basically the same amount as [thing=136063][/thing].

Tell that its sculptor well those passions read
Which yet survive, stamped on these lifeless things,
The hand that mocked them and the heart that fed.
And on the pedestal these words appear:
`My name is Ozymandias, King of Kings:
Look on my works, ye mighty, and despair!'
Nothing beside remains. Round the decay
Of that colossal wreck, boundless and bare,
The lone and level sands stretch far away".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This one caught me by surprise. I am not a fan of co-op games. With the exception of Hanabi, most of the co-op games have failed to excite me (see Shadows over Camelot). Either the games were too long, too complicated or the theme just does not sit well with my crowd (see Battlestar Galactica). So, forbidden desert was just the right mix of easy rule set, quick play time and still had enough tension. With two, the game moved along swiftly and we were done in 30 min. Even though the game was easily completed, there was always a slight tinge of danger that one of us wouldn't make it. 

This one is a keeper, and that says quite a bit about my taste of co-op games.  

After another 2 games, I have bumped this up to 9. I don't know what it is, but the short playing time coupled with the tension of finding the objects and getting back to the launch pad really made this game exciting! I think Pandemic was a game I enjoyed but because of its length, I shied away from it. Forbidden Desert just hit the sweet spot of length and depth of game play. That really is saying a lot since I don't even like co-ops that much. What a great design.

Tyler
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Okay, mark this up as a weird one for me: I don't really like Pandemic. I think it's a solid game design but something about it just doesn't make for an enjoyable game. I also wasn't terribly impressed by Forbidden Island. Nice components and simple mechanisms...but again, not terribly exciting to play.

So, along comes Forbidden Desert and I'm thinking it would just be yet another "looks cool but where's the fun?" game. Yet, to my complete surprise, this game really intrigues me. I don't know if it's the shift in dynamic making the game more of a scavenger hunt, or if it's the idea of the sand piling up and the moving storm but something about this game transforms it into a delightfully tense experience.

It's difficult but, as will become evident by a few other games higher up my list, I've never been one to shy from a challenging game.

Score one (finally) for Mr. Leacock in my book! Now, where's my canteen? It's getting hot out here!

RATING: 7
Co-op worker placement tile discovery game. We are a team of specialists sent on a desert research & recovery mission of a strange technology.  A sand storm hits and our helicopter crash lands. It quickly turns to a survival mission with limited water. Finding that alien artifact may be our only hope. Easy to teach and the theme is rich and infectious. The shifting sands adds urgency to excatvating the 5x5 modular tile desert.  Game has a small footprint. Good for the camper.  Not many components, still surprisingly inexpensive?

RATING: 6.744
In Forbidden Island, your titles sink and then disappear.  In Forbidden dessert, they shift around and get sand tiles heaped on top of them.  In addition to this, there's a thirst mechanic where you have to find water and keep hydrated or your characters will die, which is a good substitute for the 'island disappearing around you' mechanic of the first game.  If you enjoy Forbidden Island but want something a smidge (and only a smidge) more complex, try this.

RATING: 8
More interesting and challenging than forbidden island, and plays with 5.

I think out of the two Island is the better game because you have to work together to get cards to each other, a logistics puzzle I like, whereas in Desert you can all be in different areas (although the water sharing mitigates this a bit I guess). I think it's worth having both, but only because I have no other co-op games.

RATING: 7
Played twice so far. Fun game, with the Castle Panic stress at the end of your turn when you have to determine what bad stuff is going to happen to you. I like the mechanic of finding artifact locations by plotting the intersection of two card pointers. The designers also did a great job of keeping the intensity high with the storm movement, and burying tiles with sand. 

The water-carrier feels a bit over powered, but we might not have been playing correctly.

Probably won't be a hit with the entire family because of the stress factor. But it's very enjoyable and fun.

RATING: 7
Forbidden Island isn't bad, but there's not much reason to buy it if you already own Pandemic - even for families.  The games are just too similar.

Forbidden Desert, though, is different enough from Pandemic that it's worth owning.  The way the item locations are determined is neat, and the storm and water mechanics are both imaginative and thematic.  Plus, you get to complete a snap-together airship with found loot.

I'd love to trade Forbidden Island for the sandier version, if I could.

RATING: 9
The theme on this game is spectacular and the board is dynamic and really immersive. Nothing like it. Turn between players are usually pretty fast, and there are many valid options a player can take during their turn, which allows for more non-linear independent from group  play.

The instructions are very lengthy, the game is simple enough to play, but it took a good 20 minute read of the instructions to setup the game.

RATING: 7.5
Relatively easy to learn, but difficult to play. Challenging, and the moving board is rather unique (and spoils all your best laid plans!). Some roles do better in 2-player games (such as the Meteorologist, in my opinion) while others do better with more players (especially the Water Carrier). The game seems to be easier with fewer players - I have managed to beat this game on Elite with 2-players (using the Climber and the Meteorologist), but we can't even beat Normal difficulty with 3 players or more.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Co-operative, simple, yet challenging game. It feels like an accomplishment when you win. This is definitively a step up from Forbidden Island in terms of complexity and difficulty. I love having to locate the ship, but the water bearer seems to be a required character IMO. Everyone I've played this with loves it. I can't say I'd ever turn down a game if asked. Has the right balance of difficulty (with the ability to increase the difficulty) and ease of play/weight of tactics.

Artwork- 9/10
Mechanics- 8/10
Theme- 7/10
Fun- 7.5/10

RATING: 7
I played this after having played Pandemic a few times with my wife. I personally prefer this to Pandemic for 2 player games. The set up is much simpler, and the game moves quite fast. The moving tile/storm element really makes this game extremely interesting, and I really appreciate the element of luck/randomness. I'm not quite sure how it scales with more players, but I'd be happy to try it out.

RATING: 7
The framework of this game is pleasantly familiar from Pandemic and Forbidden Island.  The way the goal items and moving storm make it more of treasure hunt is a nice change to make it refreshingly its own game.  My only concern is that the best part of the other games is the "smart" deck that hits you where it hurts over and over again.  The threat of the storm is just so much more random that its hard to reason against or feel strongly threatened by.  Admittedly I've only played on the lowest difficulty level with my 4 year old so far so time will tell.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
My wife and I purchased this game, hoping that we would enjoy it as much as we enjoy playing Pandemic with 2 players. 

Turns out the game is just O.K. for 2 players, in our experience. After playing through it a handful of times together, we haven't picked it up to play just the two of us.

However, where this game shines is when we have company over who may not be as serious gamers as my wife and I. The rules are simple and the cooperative nature of the game makes for a great social interaction.

I don't know that I'll ever reach for this again when it is just my wife and I looking to play a game, but I expect it to be something we regularly reach for when company visits.

RATING: N/A
[b]1st play, 2p[/b]:

A simple cooperative game with interesting mechanics and lots of potential, but unfortunately the overpowered [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/981733/navigator-climber-superpowered]navigator & climber role combination[/url] we chose to play with exposed some cracks in the gameplay. I'll have to try again with a higher difficulty, a larger group and/or make sure never to play with that specific role combination in a future 2p game. Gorgeous components, but slightly cumbersome irregularly-sized tin.

Initial rating: [b]6.5[/b]

----

[b]No longer in my collection[/b]:

Yeah, that broken combination pretty much ruined it for me and there really wan't anything I found that made me want to go back to it. It was pretty flat unfortunately.
